ğŸ“‹ RECOMMENDATIONS
==================

âœ… Best Practices:
   1. Use ask() for operations that require a response (queries, calculations)
   2. Use tell() for fire-and-forget operations (logging, notifications)
   3. Cache actor refs to avoid repeated lookups
   4. Use parallel ask() calls when querying multiple services
   5. Consider timeouts for ask() operations in production

ğŸ”§ Code Examples:
   // Create actor ref once:
   let location = registry.lookup("database_service").await?;
   let conn = registry.get_connection(peer_addr).await?;

   // Sequential queries:
   let result1 = conn.ask(query1).await?;
   let result2 = conn.ask(query2).await?;

   // Parallel queries:
   let (r1, r2) = tokio::join!(
       conn1.ask(query1),
       conn2.ask(query2)
   );

âš ï¸  NOTE: Current ask() implementation returns mock responses.
   In production, implement proper request-response correlation.

ğŸ¯ SUMMARY AND RECOMMENDATIONS
==============================

âœ… Connection Pool API Benefits:
   1. **tell() - Fire-and-forget**: Automatic detection works with single messages, arrays, and batches
   2. **ask() - Request-response**: Simple API for synchronous communication patterns
   3. **Performance**: Batching provides 3.4x-3.7x speedup for multiple messages
   4. **Shared Infrastructure**: Same connection pool handles gossip, application data, and request-response
   5. **Type Safety**: Compile-time guarantees with ergonomic API

ğŸ“‹ When to Use tell() (Fire-and-forget):
   - âœ… Notifications and events
   - âœ… Logging and metrics
   - âœ… Multiple small messages (use batching)
   - âœ… High-throughput data streaming

ğŸ“‹ When to Use ask() (Request-response):
   - âœ… API calls requiring responses
   - âœ… Database queries
   - âœ… Configuration requests
   - âœ… Health checks and status queries

ğŸ“‹ When to Use Batching:
   - âœ… Multiple small messages (chat, notifications, logs)
   - âœ… File transfers with multiple files
   - âœ… Bulk data operations
   - âœ… High-frequency updates

ğŸ”§ API Usage Examples:
   // Fire-and-forget (tell):
   conn.tell(data).await?;                    // Single message
   conn.tell(&[&data1, &data2]).await?;      // Batch (auto-detected)
   conn.tell(TellMessage::batch(vec![&data1, &data2])).await?;
   
   // Request-response (ask):
   let response = conn.ask(request).await?;   // Returns Vec<u8>
   
   // Mixed patterns:
   conn.tell(notification).await?;           // Send notification
   let status = conn.ask(health_check).await?; // Get status

ğŸ“‹ RECOMMENDATIONS
==================

âœ… Best Practices:
   1. Do lookup() once and save actor refs for repeated communication
   2. Group messages by destination actor for batch sending
   3. Use tell() for fire-and-forget, ask() for request-response
   4. For high-throughput scenarios, batching provides 2x-33x improvement

ğŸ”§ Code Examples:
   // Create actor ref once:
   let location = registry.lookup("chat_service").await?;
   let conn = registry.get_connection(peer_addr).await?;
   let chat_ref = ActorRef { location, conn };

   // Use actor ref for all messages:
   chat_ref.conn.tell(message1).await?;
   chat_ref.conn.tell(message2).await?;

   // Or batch messages:
   let messages = vec![msg1, msg2, msg3];
   chat_ref.conn.tell(TellMessage::batch(messages)).await?;
